1.DIFFERENTITATION

: HINTS AND SOLUTIONS :
1

(d)

We have,


$$y = \cos{2\ x}\cos{3\ x} = \frac{1}{2}\left\lbrack \cos{5\ x} + \cos\text{\ x} \right\rbrack$$


$$\therefore y_{n} = \frac{1}{2}\left\{ \frac{d^{n}}{dx^{n}}\left( \cos{5\ x} \right) + \frac{d^{n}}{dx^{n}}\left( \cos x \right) \right\}$$


$$\Rightarrow y_{n} = \frac{1}{2}\left\{ 5^{n}\cos{\left( \frac{\text{n\ π}}{2} + 5\ x \right) + \cos\left( \frac{\text{n\ π}}{2} + x \right)} \right\}$$

Put t = tan θ in both the equations, we get


$$x = \frac{1 - \tan^{2}\theta}{1 + \tan^{2}\theta} = \cos{2\theta}\ldots(i)$$

and $y = \frac{2\tan\theta}{1 + \tan^{2}\theta} = \sin{2\theta\ldots(ii)}$

On differentiating both the Eqs.(i) and (ii), we get


$$\frac{\text{dx}}{d\theta} = - 2\sin{2\text{θ\ and}\frac{\text{dy}}{d\theta} = 2\cos{2\theta}}$$

Therefore, $\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\frac{\text{dy}}{d\theta}}{\frac{\text{dx}}{d\theta}} = - \frac{\cos{2\theta}}{\sin{2\theta}} = - \frac{x}{y}$

(b)


$$5f\left( x \right) + 3f\left( \frac{1}{x} \right) = x + 2\ \ldots(i)$$

On replacing x by $\frac{1}{x}$, we get


$$5f\left( \frac{1}{x} \right) + 3f\left( x \right) = \frac{1}{x} + 2\ \ldots(ii)$$

On multiplying Eq. (i) by 5 and Eq. (ii) by 3 and then on subtracting, we get


$$\therefore 16f\left( x \right) = 5x - \frac{3}{x} + 4$$


$$\Rightarrow xf\left( x \right) = \frac{5x^{2} - 3 + 4x}{16} = y$$


$$\therefore\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{10x + 4}{16}$$


$$\left. \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right|_{x = 1} = \frac{10 + 4}{16} = \frac{7}{8}$$

(b)

We have,


$$y = \log_{x^{2} + 4}\left( 7x^{2} - 5x + 1 \right) = \frac{\log_{e}\left( 7x^{2} - 5x + 1 \right)}{\log_{e}\left( x^{2} + 4 \right)} = \frac{\log_{e}{f(x)}}{\log_{e}{g(x)}}$$


$$\therefore\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\log_{e}{(g(x)} \bullet \frac{f'(x)}{f(x)} - \log_{e}{f\left( x \right)} \bullet \frac{g'(x)}{g(x)}}{\left( \log_{e}{g(x)} \right)^{2}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{\log_{e}{g(x)}}\left\{ \frac{f'(x)}{f(x)} - y\frac{g'(x)}{g(x)} \right\}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{\log_{e}{(x^{2} + 4)}}\left\{ \frac{14x - 5}{7x^{2} - 5x + 1} - \frac{2xy}{x^{2} + 4} \right\}$$

∴bysymmctry.


$$y_{n} = \frac{\left( - 1 \right)^{n - 1}\left( n - 1 \right)!}{x^{n}}$$

$$\frac{d^{2}u}{ds^{2}} = 2\left( \frac{\text{dx}}{\text{ds}} \right)^{2} + 2x\frac{d^{2}x}{ds^{2}} + 2\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{ds}} \right)^{2} + 2y\left( \frac{d^{2}y}{ds^{2}} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}u}{ds^{2}} = 2\left( 1 \right)^{2} + 2x\left( 0 \right) + 2\left( 2 \right)^{2} + 2y\left( 0 \right) = 2 + 8 = 10$$

(a)


$$f\left( x \right) = (\log_{\cot x}{\tan{x)(\log_{\tan x}{\cot{x\left. \ \right)^{- 1}} + \text{ta}n^{- 1}\frac{4x}{4 - x^{2}}}}}$$


$$= \frac{\log{\tan x}}{\log{\cot x}}.\frac{\log{\tan x}}{\log{\cot x}} + \tan^{- 1}{}\left( \frac{4x}{4 - x^{2}} \right)$$


$$= \frac{(\log{\tan{x\left. \ \right)^{2}}}}{\left( - \log{\tan x} \right)^{2}} + \tan^{- 1}{}\left( \frac{4x}{4 - x^{2}} \right)$$


$$= 1 + \tan^{- 1}\left( \frac{4x}{4 - x^{2}} \right)$$


$$\therefore f^{'}\left( x \right) = \frac{1}{1 + \left( \frac{4x}{4 - x^{2}} \right)^{2}}.\frac{\left( 4 - x^{2} \right)4 - 4x( - 2x)}{\left( 4 - x^{2} \right)^{2}}$$


$$= \frac{16 - 4x^{2} + 8x^{2}}{\left( 4 - x \right)^{2} + 16x^{2}} = \frac{4(4 + x^{2})}{\left( 4 - x^{2} \right)^{2} + \left( 4x \right)^{2}}$$

Hence, $f\left( 2 \right) = \frac{4(4 + 4)}{0 + \left( 8 \right)^{2}} = \frac{32}{64} = \frac{1}{2}$

(a)

Let y = f(tan x) and u = g(sec x)

On differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = f^{'}(\tan{x)\sec^{2}x}$$

and $\frac{\text{du}}{\text{dx}} = g^{'}(\sec{x)\sec{x\tan x}}$


$$\therefore\ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{du}} = \frac{dy\ /dx}{du\ /dx} = \frac{f^{'}(\tan{x)\sec^{2}x}}{g^{'}(\sec{x)\sec{\text{x\ }\text{tan\ }x}}}$$


$$\therefore\ \ \left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{du}} \right)_{x = \frac{\pi}{4}} = \frac{f^{'}\left( \tan\frac{\pi}{4} \right)}{g^{'}(\sec{\frac{\pi}{4})\sin\frac{\pi}{4}}}$$


$$= \frac{f^{'}\left( 1 \right).\sqrt{2}}{g^{'}(\sqrt{2)}} = \frac{2.\sqrt{2}}{4} = \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$$

$$= \ \frac{1 - \log_{e}{\log_{e}x}}{x({\log_{e}{x)}}^{2}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \ f^{'}\left( e \right) = \frac{1 - \log_{e}{\log_{e}e}}{e{(\log_{e}{e)}}^{2}} = \frac{1 - \log_{e}1}{e} = \frac{1}{e}$$

$$2^{x}\log{2 + 2^{y}\log{2\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = 2^{x + y}\log{2\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)}}}$$


$$\Rightarrow 2^{x} + 2^{y}\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \ 2^{x + y}\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \ 2^{x} - 2^{x + y} = \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}}\left( 2^{x + y} - 2^{y} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow {\ 2}^{x - y}\frac{(1 - 2^{y})}{(2^{x} - 1)} = \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}}$$

We have,


$$y = \sin^{- 1}\left( \frac{\sin\alpha\sin x}{1 - \cos\alpha\sin x} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{\sqrt{1 - \frac{\sin^{2}\alpha\sin^{2}x}{\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)^{2}}}}\frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( \frac{\sin\alpha\sin x}{1 - \cos\alpha\sin x} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)}{\sqrt{1 + \sin^{2}x - 2\cos\alpha\sin x}} \bullet \frac{\sin\alpha}{\cos\alpha}\frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( 1 - \frac{1}{1 - \cos\alpha\sin x} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = - \frac{\tan\alpha\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)}{\sqrt{1 + \sin^{2}x - 2\cos\alpha\sin x}}\frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( 1 - \frac{1}{1 - \cos\alpha\sin x} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\tan\alpha\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)}{\sqrt{1 + \sin^{2}x - 2\sin x\cos\alpha}}\left\{ \frac{1 - \cos\alpha\cos x}{\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)^{2}} \right\}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\sin\alpha\cos x}{\left( 1 - \cos\alpha\sin x \right)\sqrt{1 + \sin^{2}x - 2\cos\alpha\sin x}}$$


$$\therefore\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)_{x = 0} = \sin\alpha \Rightarrow y^{'}\left( 0 \right) = \sin\alpha$$

and y = 2sin θ − sin 2θ


$$\frac{\text{dx}}{d\theta} = \ - 2\sin{\theta + 2\sin{2\theta}}$$

and $\frac{\text{dy}}{d\theta} = 2\cos{\theta - 2\cos{2\theta}}$


$$\therefore\ \ \ \ \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{2\cos{\theta - 2\cos{2\theta}}}{- 2\sin{\theta + 2\sin{2\theta}}}$$


$$= \frac{cos\theta - \cos{2\theta}}{\sin{2\theta - \sin\theta}}$$


$$= \frac{2\sin{\left( \frac{\theta + 2\theta}{2} \right)\sin\left( \frac{2\theta - \theta}{2} \right)}}{2\cos\left( \frac{\theta + 2\theta}{2} \right)\sin\left( \frac{2\theta - \theta}{2} \right)} = \tan\frac{3\theta}{2}$$

 =  − 16cos 4x − 4cos 2x =  − 4(cos 2x + 4cos 4x)

f″(x) = n(n−1)xn − 2 ⇒  f″(1) = n(n−1)


  … … … … …  … …


…  … … … …  … … 


fn(x) = n(n−1)(n−2)…2.1


⇒  fn(1) = n(n−1)(n−2)…2.1

Now, $f\left( 1 \right) - \frac{f^{'}(1)}{1!} + \frac{f^{''}(1)}{2!} - \frac{f^{'''}(1)}{3!} + ... + \frac{\left( - 1 \right)^{n}f^{n}(1)}{n!}$


$$= 1 - \frac{n}{1!} + \frac{n\left( n - 1 \right)}{2!} - \frac{n\left( n - 1 \right)\left( n - 2 \right)}{3!}\ + ... + \frac{\left( - 1 \right)^{n}n\left( n - 1 \right)\left( n - 2 \right)\ldots 2.1}{n!}$$


 = (1−1)n = 0

f″(x) = 6x + 2a


f‴(x) = 6


∴ a = f′(1) = 3 + 2a + b

b = 12 + 2a

 ⇒  − 2a + b = 12…(ii)

and c = 6 …(iii)

On solving Eqs. (i), (ii) and (iii), we get

a =  − 5, b = 2 and c = 6


∴ f(x) = x3 − 5x2 + 2x + 6

Thus, f(0) = 6, f(1) = 4, f(2) =  − 2, f(3) =  − 6

On differentiating Eq. (i) w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}} = e^{t}(\cos{t - \sin{t)}}$$

and $\frac{\text{dx}}{\text{dt}} = e^{t}(\sin{t + \cos{t)}}$


$$\therefore\ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}}}{\frac{\text{dx}}{\text{dt}}} = \frac{\cos{t - \sin t}}{\cos{t + \sin t}}$$

Again differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{d}{\text{dt}}\left( \frac{\cos{t - \sin t}}{\cos{t - \sin t}} \right)\frac{\text{dt}}{\text{dx}}$$


$$= \left\lbrack \frac{\begin{matrix} \lbrack(\cos{t + \sin{t)( - \sin{t - \cos{t) -}}}} \\ {(cos}{t - \sin{t)( - \sin{t + \cos{t)\rbrack}}}} \\ \end{matrix}}{(\cos{t + \sin{t\left. \ \right)^{2}}}} \right\rbrack\frac{\text{dt}}{\text{dx}}$$


$$= \frac{- 2}{\left( \cos{t + \sin t} \right)^{2}}.\frac{1}{e^{t}(\sin{t + \cos{t)}}}$$


$$= \ \ \frac{- 2}{(e^{t}\cos{t + e^{t}\sin{t)}}}.\frac{1}{\left( \cos{t + \sin t} \right)^{2}}$$


$$= \frac{- 2}{x + y}.\frac{1}{(\cos{t + \sin{t\left. \ \right)^{2}}}}\ \ \lbrack from\ Eq.(i)\rbrack$$

At $t = \frac{\pi}{4},x = 1,\ y = 1$


$$\therefore\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{- 2}{1 + 1}.\frac{1}{\left( \cos\frac{\pi}{4} + \sin\frac{\pi}{4} \right)^{2}}$$


$$= \frac{- 1}{\left\lbrack \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} + \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \right\rbrack} = - \frac{1}{2}$$

(a)

We have,


$$y = \tan^{- 1}\left( \frac{\sqrt{1 + x^{2}} - 1}{x} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow y = \tan^{- 1}\left( \frac{\sec\theta - 1}{\tan\theta} \right),\ \text{where}\ x = \tan\theta$$


$$\Rightarrow y = \tan^{- 1}\left( \frac{1 - \cos\theta}{\sin\theta} \right) = \tan^{- 1}\left( \tan\frac{\theta}{2} \right) = \frac{1}{2}\theta = \frac{1}{2}\tan^{- 1}x$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{2\left( 1 + x^{2} \right)} \Rightarrow \left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)_{x = 0} = \frac{1}{2}$$

(a)

Given, $y^{2} = ax^{2} + bx + c \Rightarrow 2y\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = 2ax + b$


$$\ \Rightarrow 2\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)^{2} + 2y\left( \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} \right) = 2a\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ $$


$$\Rightarrow y\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = a - \left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)^{2}$$


$$\Rightarrow y\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = a - \left( \frac{2ax + b}{2y} \right)^{2}$$


$$\Rightarrow \ y\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{4ay^{2} - \left( 2ax + b \right)^{2}}{4y^{2}}$$


$$\Rightarrow 4y^{3}\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = 4a\left( ax^{2} + bx + c \right) - (4a^{2}x^{2} + 4abx + b^{2})$$


$$\Rightarrow 4y^{3}\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = 4ac - b^{2}$$

$\Rightarrow y^{3}\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{4ac - b^{2}}{4} =$constant

(b)

We have,


$$x = a\cos t + \frac{b}{2}\cos{2t},\ y = a\sin t + \frac{b}{2}\sin{2t}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = - a\sin t - b\sin{2t},\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}} = a\cos t + b\cos{2t}$$


$$\therefore\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{dy/dt}{dx/dt} = \frac{a\cos t + b\cos{2t}}{- a\sin t - b\sin{2t}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = - \frac{\left( a\cos t + b\cos{2t} \right)}{\left( a\sin t + b\sin{2t} \right)}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right) = \frac{d}{\text{dt}}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}} \right) \bullet \frac{\text{dt}}{\text{dx}} = - \frac{d}{\text{dt}}\frac{\left( a\cos t + b\cos{2t} \right)}{\left( a\sin t + b\sin{2t} \right)} \bullet \frac{\text{dt}}{\text{dx}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = - \left\lbrack \frac{a^{2} + 2b^{2} + 3ab\cos t}{\left( a\sin t + b\sin{2t} \right)^{3}} \right\rbrack$$


$$\therefore\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = 0 \Rightarrow a^{2} + 2b^{2} + 3ab\cos t = 0 \Rightarrow \cos t = - \left( \frac{a^{2} + 2b^{2}}{3ab} \right)$$

$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = 2x\tan{(\log{x) + x\sec^{2}{(\log{x) + 2x}}}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = 2x\lbrack 1 + \tan{(\log{x)\rbrack + x\sec^{2}{(\log{x)}}}}$$

$$\Rightarrow \frac{d}{\text{dx}}f\left( x \right) = \left| \begin{matrix} 3x^{2} & 4x^{3} & 6x \\ 1 & - 6 & 4 \\ p & p^{2} & p^{3} \\ \end{matrix} \right|$$

Given, sin (x + y) + cos (x+y) = log (x + y)

$$\cos{\left( x + y \right)\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right) - \sin{\left( x + y \right)\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)}}$$


$$= \frac{1}{\left( x + y \right)}\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = 0\ \ \Rightarrow \ \ \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = 0\ \ \ \ \ $$

(c)

We have,

y = esin − 1x and u = log x


$$\therefore\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{e^{\sin^{- 1}x}}{\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}},\frac{\text{du}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{x} \Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{du}} = \frac{\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}}}{\frac{\text{du}}{\text{dx}}} = \frac{\text{x\ }e^{\sin^{- 1}x}}{\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}}$$

(b)

Given, y = xlog x

On differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{x}{x} + \log x$$


$$\Rightarrow \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \log{e + \log x}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \log{(\text{ex})}$$

(a)


x = a(1 + cos θ),     y = a(θ + sin θ)


$$\frac{\text{dx}}{d\theta} = - {a\text{\ sin}}{\theta,}\frac{\text{dy}}{d\theta} = a\ (1 + \cos{\theta)}$$

$\therefore\ \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}}\ = \ \frac{1 + \cos\theta}{- \sin\theta}$ = $\frac{2\cos^{2}\frac{\theta}{2}}{- 2\sin{\frac{\theta}{2}\cos\frac{\theta}{2}}}$


$$\Rightarrow \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \ - \cot\frac{\theta}{2}$$


$$\therefore\ \ \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right) = \frac{d}{d\theta}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right).\frac{\text{dθ}}{\text{dx}}$$

$= \frac{d}{d\theta}\left( - \cot\frac{\theta}{2} \right).\frac{1}{- a\sin\theta}$


$$= \frac{1}{2}\text{cose}c^{2}\frac{\theta}{2}.\frac{1}{- a\sin\theta}$$


$$\ \ \therefore\ \ \left( \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} \right)_{\theta = \frac{\pi}{2}} = \frac{1}{2}.2.\frac{1}{- a} = - \frac{1}{a}$$

(b)

Let f(x) = |x−1| + |x − 5|


$$f\left( x \right) = \left\{ \begin{matrix} - \left( x - 1 \right) - \left( x - 5 \right), & x < 1 \\ \left( x - 1 \right) - \left( x - 5 \right), & 1 \leq x \leq 5 \\ x - 1 + x - 5, & x > 5 \\ \end{matrix} \right.\ $$


$$f\left( x \right) = \left\{ \begin{matrix} \begin{matrix} 6 - 2x, & x < 1 \\ 4, & x \leq 5 \\ \end{matrix} \\ 2x - 6,\ \ \ x > 5 \\ \end{matrix} \right.\ $$


∵x = 3 ∈ (1, 5)

∴ For x = 3,


f(x) = 4 ⇒ f′(x) = 0

(d)

Let u = sin2x and v = cos2x

On differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{du}}{\text{dx}} = 2\sin{x\cos{x = \sin{2x}}}$$

and $\frac{\text{dv}}{\text{dx}} = - 2\cos{x\sin{x = - \sin{2x}}}$


$$\therefore\frac{\text{du}}{\text{dv}} = \frac{du/dx}{dv/dx} = \frac{\sin{2x}}{- \sin{2x}} = - 1$$

(b)


f(x) = exand g(x) = sin − 1x

and h(x) = f[g(x)]


 ⇒ h(x) = f(sin − 1x) = esin − 1x


∴ h(x) = esin − 1x


$$\Rightarrow h^{'}\left( x \right) = e^{\sin^{- 1}x}\frac{1}{\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{h^{'}(x)}{h(x)} = \frac{1}{\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}}$$

(a)

Let $y = \sin^{- 1}\left( \frac{\sqrt{1 + x} + \sqrt{1 - x}}{2} \right)$

Putting x = cos θ, we get


$$y = \sin^{- 1}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\cos\frac{\theta}{2} + \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\sin\frac{\theta}{2} \right) = \sin^{- 1}\left\{ \sin\left( \frac{\pi}{4} + \frac{\theta}{2} \right) \right\}$$


$$\Rightarrow y = \frac{\pi}{4} + \frac{1}{2}\theta = \frac{\pi}{4} + \frac{1}{2}\cos^{- 1}x$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = - \frac{1}{2\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}}$$

(d)


h′(x) = [f(x)2 + g(x)2]


⇒  h″(x) = 2f(x)f′(x) + 2g(x)g′(x)


$$\begin{bmatrix} \because g\left( x \right) = f^{'}\left( x \right) \\ \Rightarrow g^{'}\left( x \right) = f^{''}\left( x \right) \\ \end{bmatrix}$$


∴ h″(x) = 2f(x)g(x) + 2g(x)(−f(x))


[∵f″(x) =  − f(x)]


 ⇒ h″(x) = 0

 ⇒ h′(x) = C, a constant for all x ∈ R


⇒ h(x) = Cx + C1


 ⇒ h(0) = C1and h(1) = C + C1


 ⇒ 2 = C1and 8 = C + C1


 ⇒ C1 = 2 and C = 6


∴ h(x) = 6x + 2


 ⇒ h(2) = 6 × 2 + 2 = 14

(a)

We have,


xpyq = (x+y)p + q


 ⇒ plog x + qlog y = (p+q)log (x+y)

Diff w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{p}{x} + \frac{q}{y}\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{p + q}{x + y}\left( 1 + \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}}\left( \frac{q}{y} - \frac{p + q}{x + y} \right) \Rightarrow \frac{p + q}{x + y} - \frac{p}{x} \Rightarrow \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{y}{x}$$

(c)

Let y = (x+1)n


$$\therefore\ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = n\left( x + 1 \right)^{n - 1}$$


$$\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = n\left( n - 1 \right)\left( x + 1 \right)^{n - 2}$$

Similarly, $\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{n}} = n\left( n - 1 \right)\left( n - 2 \right)\ldots 3.2.1 = n!$

(b)

Since, $\sin^{- 1}{x = \frac{\pi}{2} - \sin^{- 1}y}$


 ⇒ sin − 1x = cos − 1y


$$\Rightarrow \ \ y = \ \sqrt{1 - x^{2}}(\because\sin^{- 1}{x = \cos^{- 1}\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}})$$

On differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{1}{2\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}}\left( - 2x \right) = - \frac{x}{y}$$

(d)

We have,


x = etsin tand y = etcos t

$\Rightarrow \frac{\text{dx}}{\text{dt}} = e^{t}\left( \sin t + \cos t \right)$ and $\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}} = e^{t}\left( \cos t - \sin t \right)$


$$\therefore\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \frac{\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dt}}}{\frac{\text{dx}}{\text{dt}}} = \frac{\cos t - \sin t}{\cos t + \sin t}$$

Now, $\frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{d}{\text{dx}}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right) = \frac{d}{\text{dt}}\left( \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} \right)\frac{\text{dt}}{\text{dx}}$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{d}{\text{dt}}\left( \frac{\cos t - \sin t}{\cos t + \sin t} \right) \times \frac{1}{e^{t}\left( \sin t + \cos t \right)}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{- \left( \cos t + \sin t \right)^{2} - \left( \cos t - \sin t \right)^{2}}{\left( \cos t + \sin t \right)^{2}} \times \frac{1}{e^{t}\left( \cos t + \sin t \right)}$$


$$\Rightarrow \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} = \frac{- 2}{\left( \cos t + \sin t \right)^{3}e^{t}} \Rightarrow \left( \frac{d^{2}y}{dx^{2}} \right)_{t = \pi} = \frac{- 2}{- e^{\pi}} = \frac{2}{e^{\pi}}$$
351

(d)

Since, $y = \sqrt{\frac{1 - x}{1 + x}}$

On differentiating w.r.t. x, we get


$$\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = \ \frac{\sqrt{1 + x} \times \frac{( - 1)}{2\sqrt{1 - x}} - \sqrt{1 - x} \times \frac{1}{2\sqrt{1 + x}}}{{(\sqrt{1 + x})}^{2}}$$


$$\Rightarrow \ \ \ \frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} = - \frac{1}{\left( 1 + x \right)\sqrt{1 - x^{2}}} \times \frac{1 - x}{1 - x}$$


$$\Rightarrow \ \left( 1 - x^{2} \right)\frac{\text{dy}}{\text{dx}} + y = 0\ $$
